   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Near-death experience
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near_death_experience&amp;redirect=no" title="Near death experience">
       Near death experience
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="hatnote">
      For other uses, see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-death_experience_(disambiguation)" title="Near-death experience (disambiguation)">
       Near-death experience (disambiguation)
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      "NDE" redirects here. For other uses, see
      <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/NDE_(disambiguation)" title="NDE (disambiguation)">
       NDE (disambiguation)
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      "Near death" redirects here. For the comic book, see
      <a href="/wiki/Near_Death_(comics)" title="Near Death (comics)">
       Near Death (comics)
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <b>
       near-death experience
      </b>
      (
      <b>
       NDE
      </b>
      ) is a personal
      <a href="/wiki/Experience" title="Experience">
       experience
      </a>
      associated with impending
      <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">
       death
      </a>
      , encompassing multiple possible sensations including detachment from the body, feelings of levitation, total serenity, security, warmth, the experience of absolute dissolution, and the presence of a light.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-overview-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britton.26Bootzin_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Britton.26Bootzin-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Explanatory models for the NDE can be divided into several broad categories, including
      <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">
       psychological
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">
       physiological
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Transcendence_(philosophy)" title="Transcendence (philosophy)">
       transcendental
      </a>
      explanations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-overview-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Research from
      <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">
       neuroscience
      </a>
      considers the NDE to be a hallucination caused by various physiological and psychological factors,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while some NDE researchers in the field of
      <a href="/wiki/Near-death_studies" title="Near-death studies">
       near-death studies
      </a>
      advocate for a transcendental explanation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-overview-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-horizonresearch.org_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-horizonresearch.org-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www-new1.heacademy.ac.uk_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-www-new1.heacademy.ac.uk-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">
       Characteristics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Characteristics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7867" data-file-width="3444" height="503" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg/220px-Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg/330px-Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg/440px-Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hieronymus_Bosch_013.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Ascent_of_the_Blessed" title="Ascent of the Blessed">
          Ascent of the Blessed
         </a>
        </i>
        by
        <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_Bosch" title="Hieronymus Bosch">
         Hieronymus Bosch
        </a>
        is associated by some NDE researchers with aspects of the NDE.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lommel2010_10-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Lommel2010-10">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          10
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
         <a href="#cite_note-11">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          11
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The equivalent
      <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
       French
      </a>
      term
      <i>
       exprience de mort imminente
      </i>
      (experience of imminent death) was proposed by the French
      <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">
       psychologist
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">
       epistemologist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Egger" title="Egger">
       Victor Egger
      </a>
      as a result of discussions in the 1890s among
      <a href="/wiki/Philosopher" title="Philosopher">
       philosophers
      </a>
      and psychologists concerning climbers' stories of the panoramic life review during falls.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1968
      <a href="/wiki/Celia_Green" title="Celia Green">
       Celia Green
      </a>
      published an analysis of 400 first-hand accounts of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out-of-body_experiences" title="Out-of-body experiences">
       out-of-body experiences
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This represented the first attempt to provide a
      <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(general)" title="Taxonomy (general)">
       taxonomy
      </a>
      of such experiences, viewed simply as anomalous perceptual experiences, or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hallucinations" title="Hallucinations">
       hallucinations
      </a>
      . These experiences were popularized by the work of
      <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">
       psychiatrist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Moody" title="Raymond Moody">
       Raymond Moody
      </a>
      in 1975 as the near-death experience (NDE).
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">
       Researchers
      </a>
      have identified the common elements that define near-death experiences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Greyson" title="Bruce Greyson">
       Bruce Greyson
      </a>
      argues that the general features of the experience include impressions of being outside one's physical body, visions of deceased relatives and religious figures, and transcendence of egotic and spatiotemporal boundaries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many common elements have been reported, although the person's interpretation of these events often corresponds with the
      <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">
       cultural
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">
       philosophical
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">
       religious
      </a>
      beliefs of the person experiencing it.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another common element in near-death experiences is encountering people, which are generally identified according to the person's individual faith; for instance, in America, where 46% of the population believes in
      <a href="/wiki/Guardian_angel" title="Guardian angel">
       guardian angels
      </a>
      , they will will often be identified as angels or deceased loved ones (or will be unidentified), while Hindus will often identify them as messengers of the god of death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-handbook-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kennard.2C_Mary_J_1998_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kennard.2C_Mary_J_1998-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is particularly true for patients in a clinical setting.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Although the features of NDEs vary from one case to the next, common traits that have been reported by NDErs are as follows:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       A sense/awareness of being dead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       A sense of
       <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">
        peace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">
        well-being
       </a>
       and painlessness. Positive
       <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">
        emotions
       </a>
       . A sense of removal from the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/Out-of-body_experience" title="Out-of-body experience">
        out-of-body experience
       </a>
       . A perception of one's body from an outside position. Sometimes observing doctors and nurses performing medical resuscitation efforts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_M._1985_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morse_M._1985-21">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         21
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       A "tunnel experience" or entering a darkness. A sense of moving up, or through, a passageway or staircase.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_M._1985_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morse_M._1985-21">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         21
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       A rapid movement toward and/or sudden immersion in a powerful light (or "Being of Light") which communicates with the person.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       An intense feeling of
       <a href="/wiki/Unconditional_love" title="Unconditional love">
        unconditional love
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Acceptance" title="Acceptance">
        acceptance
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Encountering "Beings of Light", "Beings dressed in white", or similar. Also, the possibility of being reunited with deceased loved ones.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_M._1985_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morse_M._1985-21">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         21
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Receiving a
       <a href="/wiki/Life_review" title="Life review">
        life review
       </a>
       , commonly referred to as "seeing one's life flash before one's eyes".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Receiving knowledge about one's life and the nature of the universe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Approaching a border,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lommel2_19-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-lommel2-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       or a decision by oneself or others to return to one's body, often accompanied by a reluctance to return.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANDS_20-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-IANDS-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_M._1985_21-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morse_M._1985-21">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         21
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Suddenly finding oneself back inside one's body.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         22
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Connection to the cultural beliefs held by the individual, which seem to dictate some of the phenomena experienced in the NDE and particularly the later interpretation thereof.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-handbook-17">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         17
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Ring" title="Kenneth Ring">
       Kenneth Ring
      </a>
      (1980) subdivided the NDE on a five-stage
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continuum_(theory)" title="Continuum (theory)">
       continuum
      </a>
      . The subdivisions were:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ol>
      <li>
       Peace
      </li>
      <li>
       Body separation
      </li>
      <li>
       Entering darkness
      </li>
      <li>
       Seeing the light
      </li>
      <li>
       Entering the light
      </li>
     </ol>
     <p>
      He stated that 60% experienced stage 1 (feelings of peace and contentment), but only 10% experienced stage 5 ("entering the light").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Clinical circumstances associated with near-death experiences include
      <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrest" title="Cardiac arrest">
       cardiac arrest
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">
       myocardial infarction
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Clinical_death" title="Clinical death">
       clinical death
      </a>
      ); shock in postpartum
      <a href="/wiki/Bleeding" title="Bleeding">
       loss of blood
      </a>
      or in perioperative complications; septic or anaphylactic shock; electrocution;
      <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">
       coma
      </a>
      resulting from
      <a href="/wiki/Traumatic_brain_injury" title="Traumatic brain injury">
       traumatic brain damage
      </a>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">
       intracerebral hemorrhage
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_infarction" title="Cerebral infarction">
       cerebral infarction
      </a>
      ; attempted
      <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">
       suicide
      </a>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/Drowning" title="Drowning">
       near-drowning
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Asphyxia" title="Asphyxia">
       asphyxia
      </a>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/Apnea" title="Apnea">
       apnea
      </a>
      ; and serious
      <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">
       depression
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In contrast to common belief, Kenneth Ring argues that attempted suicides do not lead more often to unpleasant NDEs than unintended near-death situations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="NDE_variants">
       NDE variants
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: NDE variants">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Some NDEs have elements that bear little resemblance to the "typical" near-death experience. Anywhere from one percent (according to a 1982 Gallup poll) to 20 percent of subjects may have distressing experiences and feel terrified or uneasy as various parts of the NDE occur, they visit or view dark and depressing areas or are accosted by what seem to be hostile or oppositional forces or presences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Persons having bad experiences were not marked by more religiosity or suicidal background. According to one study (Greyson 2006) there is little association between NDEs and prior psychiatric treatment, prior suicidal behavior, or family history of suicidal behavior. There was also little association between NDEs and religiosity, or prior brushes with death, suggesting the occurrence of NDEs is not influenced by psychopathology, by religious denomination or religiosity, or by experiencers' prior expectations of a pleasant dying process or continued postmortem existence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Greyson (2007) also found that the long term recall of NDE incidents was stable and did not change due to embellishment over time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Bush (2012), a counselor, and board member and former Executive Director to the International Association for Near-Death Studies, holds that not all negative NDE accounts are reported by people with a religious background.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Suicide attempters, who should be expected to have a higher rate of psychopathology according to Greyson (1991) did not show much difference from non-suicides in the frequency of NDEs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Research">
       Research
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Research">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Introduction">
       Introduction
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Introduction">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      As
      <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">
       cognitive neuroscience
      </a>
      is an interdisciplinary area of study embracing
      <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">
       neuroscience
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">
       psychology
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">
       computer science
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kosslyn.2C_S_1992_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kosslyn.2C_S_1992-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and NDE studies address multiple possible feelings, sensations and their origins, some research on NDEs has been conducted by researchers with credentials in cognitive neuroscience. Cognitive neuroscience addresses the questions of how psychological functions (for example, human feelings and sensations) are produced by neural circuitry (including the human brain).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kosslyn.2C_S_1992_32-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kosslyn.2C_S_1992-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Modern contributions to the research on near-death experiences, however, have come from several academic disciplines that generally do not include neuroscience. There are multiple reasons for this trend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harris.2C_Sam._33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harris.2C_Sam.-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, brain activity
      <a href="/wiki/Functional_neuroimaging" title="Functional neuroimaging">
       scans
      </a>
      are not typically performed when a patient is undergoing attempts at emergency resuscitation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mobbs.2C_D_2012.2C_Page_446_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mobbs.2C_D_2012.2C_Page_446-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Claiming that there is no measurable brain activity without having a variety of different
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EEG" title="EEG">
       EEG
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CatSCAN" title="CatSCAN">
       catSCAN
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FMRI" title="FMRI">
       FMRI
      </a>
      , etc. is not considered a good scientific practice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harris.2C_Sam._33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harris.2C_Sam.-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mobbs.2C_D_2012.2C_Page_446_34-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mobbs.2C_D_2012.2C_Page_446-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Existing research is mainly in the disciplines of medicine, psychology and psychiatry. Heightened brain activity has been recorded in experimental rats directly following cardiac arrest, though there has been no similar research in humans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Individual cases of NDEs in literature have been identified into ancient times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the 19th century a few efforts moved beyond studying individual cases - one privately done by the Mormons and one in Switzerland. Up to 2005, 95% of world cultures have been documented making some mention of NDEs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 2001 study by Berlin sociologist
      <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Knoblauch" title="Hubert Knoblauch">
       Hubert Knoblauch
      </a>
      concluded that 4 percent of the German population had been through a near death experience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of the survivors of cardiac arrest, between 10% and 20% reported more or less significant near-death experiences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Contemporary interest in this field of study was originally spurred by the writings of
      <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Moody" title="Raymond Moody">
       Raymond Moody
      </a>
      's book
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Life_After_Life_(book)" title="Life After Life (book)">
        Life After Life
       </a>
      </i>
      , which was released in 1975, brought public attention to the topic of NDEs. This was soon to be followed by the establishment of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_Near-Death_Studies" title="International Association for Near-Death Studies">
       International Association for Near-Death Studies
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IANDS" title="IANDS">
       IANDS
      </a>
      ) in 1981. IANDS is an international organization that encourages scientific research and education on the physical, psychological, social, and spiritual nature and ramifications of near-death experiences. Among its publications are the peer-reviewed
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Near-Death_Studies" title="Journal of Near-Death Studies">
        Journal of Near-Death Studies
       </a>
      </i>
      and the quarterly newsletter
      <i>
       Vital Signs
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iands.org_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-iands.org-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Greyson" title="Bruce Greyson">
       Bruce Greyson
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">
       psychiatrist
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Ring" title="Kenneth Ring">
       Kenneth Ring
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">
       psychologist
      </a>
      ), and Michael Sabom (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiologist" title="Cardiologist">
       cardiologist
      </a>
      ), helped to launch the field of
      <a href="/wiki/Near-death_studies" title="Near-death studies">
       near-death studies
      </a>
      and introduced the study of near-death experiences to the academic setting. From 1975 to 2005, some 2500 self reported individuals in the US had been reviewed in retrospective studies of the phenomena
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with an additional 600 outside the US in the West,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 70 in Asia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prospective studies, reviewing groups of individuals and then finding who had an NDE after some time and costing more to do, had identified 270 individuals.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In all close to 3500 individual cases between 1975 and 2005 had been reviewed in one or another study. All these studies were carried out by some 55 researchers or teams of researchers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandBook-Field_39-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-HandBook-Field-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The medical community has been reluctant to address the phenomenon of NDEs, and grant money for research has been scarce.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iands.org_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-iands.org-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, both Greyson and Ring developed tools usable in a clinical setting. Major contributions to the field include Ring's construction of a "Weighted Core Experience Index"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to measure the depth of the near-death experience, and Greyson's construction of the "Near-death experience scale"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greyson.2C_Bruce_1983_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greyson.2C_Bruce_1983-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to differentiate between subjects that are more or less likely to have experienced an NDE. The latter scale is also, according to its author, clinically useful in differentiating NDEs from organic brain syndromes and non-specific stress responses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greyson.2C_Bruce_1983_48-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greyson.2C_Bruce_1983-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The NDE-scale was later found to fit the Rasch rating scale model.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Greyson
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      has also brought attention to the near-death experience as a focus of clinical attention, while
      <a href="/wiki/Melvin_L._Morse" title="Melvin L. Morse">
       Melvin Morse
      </a>
      , head of the Institute for the Scientific Study of Consciousness, and colleagues
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_M._1985_21-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Morse_M._1985-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      have investigated near-death experiences in a pediatric population.
     </p>
     <p>
      Neurobiological factors in the experience have been investigated by researchers in the field of medical science and psychiatry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among the researchers and commentators who tend to emphasize a naturalistic and neurological base for the experience are the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
       British
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">
       psychologist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Susan_Blackmore" title="Susan Blackmore">
       Susan Blackmore
      </a>
      (1993), with her "dying brain hypothesis",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the founding publisher of
      <a href="/wiki/Skeptic_(U.S._magazine)" title="Skeptic (U.S. magazine)">
       <i>
        Skeptic
       </i>
      </a>
      magazine,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shermer" title="Michael Shermer">
       Michael Shermer
      </a>
      (1998). More recently, cognitive neuroscientists Jason Braithwaite (2008)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Braithwaite_2008_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Braithwaite_2008-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">
       University of Birmingham
      </a>
      and Sebastian Dieguez (2008)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Olaf Blanke (2009)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecole_Polytechnique_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_Lausanne" title="Ecole Polytechnique Fdrale de Lausanne">
       Ecole Polytechnique Fdrale de Lausanne
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
       Switzerland
      </a>
      have published accounts presenting evidence for a brain-based explanation of near-death experiences.
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 2008, it was announced that 25 U.K. and U.S. hospitals would examine near-death experiences in 1,500
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_attack" title="Heart attack">
       heart attack
      </a>
      patient-survivors. The three-year study, coordinated by
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Parnia" title="Sam Parnia">
       Sam Parnia
      </a>
      at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southampton_University" title="Southampton University">
       Southampton University
      </a>
      , hopes to determine if people without
      <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_cycle" title="Cardiac cycle">
       heartbeat
      </a>
      or brain activity can have an
      <a href="/wiki/Out-of-body_experience" title="Out-of-body experience">
       out-of-body experience
      </a>
      with veridical visual perceptions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This study follows on from an earlier 18-month pilot project.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The results of the study were published in the journal Resuscitation on October 6, 2014.
     </p>
     <p>
      Most top peer-reviewed journals in neuroscience, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Nature_Reviews_Neuroscience" title="Nature Reviews Neuroscience">
       Nature Reviews Neuroscience
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_Research_Reviews" title="Brain Research Reviews">
       Brain Research Reviews
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Biological_Psychiatry" title="Biological Psychiatry">
       Biological Psychiatry
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Cognitive_Neuroscience" title="Journal of Cognitive Neuroscience">
       Journal of Cognitive Neuroscience
      </a>
      are generally not publishing research on NDEs. Among the scientific and academic journals that have published, or are regularly publishing, new research on the subject of NDEs are
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Near-Death_Studies" title="Journal of Near-Death Studies">
        Journal of Near-Death Studies
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Nervous_and_Mental_Disease" title="Journal of Nervous and Mental Disease">
        Journal of Nervous and Mental Disease
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       British Journal of Psychology
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       American Journal of Disease of Children
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Resuscitation
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">
        The Lancet
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Death Studies
      </i>
      , and the
      <i>
       Journal of Advanced Nursing
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Variance_in_NDE_studies">
       Variance in NDE studies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Variance in NDE studies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The prevalence of NDEs has been variable in the studies that have been performed. According to the Gallup and Proctor survey in 1980-1981, of a representative sample of the American population, data showed that 15% described themselves as having had an "unusual experience" when on the verge of death or having a "close call".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Knoblauch in 2001 performed a more selective study in Germany and found that 4% of the sample population had an NDE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The information gathered from these studies may nevertheless be subject to the broad timeframe and location of the investigation.
     </p>
     <p>
      Perera et al., in 2005, conducted a telephone survey of a representative sample of the Australian population, as part of the Roy Morgan Catibus Survey, and concluded that 8.9% of the population had an NDE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a clinical setting, van Lommel et al. (2001), a cardiologist from Netherlands, studied a group of patients who had suffered cardiac arrests and who were successfully revived. They found that 62 patients (18%) had an NDE, of whom 41 (12%, or 66% of those who had an NDE) described a core experience.
     </p>
     <p>
      According to Martens
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the only satisfying method to address the NDE-issue would be an international multi-centric data collection within the framework for standardized reporting of cardiac arrest events. The use of cardiac-arrest criteria as a basis for NDE research has been a common approach among the European branch of the research field.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lommel_P_2001_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lommel_P_2001-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Neurobiological_and_psychological_analysis">
       Neurobiological and psychological analysis
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Neurobiological and psychological analysis">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Psychologist
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
       Chris French
      </a>
      has summarized psychological and physiological theories that provide a physical explanation for NDEs. One psychological theory proposes that the NDE is a dissociative defense mechanism that occurs in times of extreme danger. A wide range of physiological theories of the NDE has been put forward including those based upon
      <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hypoxia" title="Cerebral hypoxia">
       cerebral hypoxia
      </a>
      , anoxia, and
      <a href="/wiki/Hypercapnia" title="Hypercapnia">
       hypercarbia
      </a>
      ; endorphins and other neurotransmitters; and abnormal activity in the
      <a href="/wiki/Temporal_lobe" title="Temporal lobe">
       temporal lobes
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1970s professor of psychiatry Russell Noyes and clinical psychologist Roy Kletti suggested the NDE is a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Depersonalization" title="Depersonalization">
       depersonalization
      </a>
      experienced under emotional conditions such as life-threatening danger and that the NDE can best be understood as a fantasy based hallucination.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the early 1980s the neuropsychologist Daniel Carr proposed that the NDE has characteristics suggestive of a limbic lobe syndrome and that the NDE can be explained by the release of
      <a href="/wiki/Endorphins" title="Endorphins">
       endorphins
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Enkephalin" title="Enkephalin">
       enkephalins
      </a>
      in the brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Judson and Wiltshaw (1983) noted how the release of endorphins can lead to blissful or emotional NDEs, whilst
      <a href="/wiki/Naloxone" title="Naloxone">
       naloxone
      </a>
      can produce "hellish" NDEs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first formal neurobiological model for NDE was presented in 1987 by Chilean scientists Juan Sebastin Gmez-Jeria (who holds a PhD in Molecular Physical Chemistry) and Juan Carlos Saavedra-Aguilar (
      <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">
       M.D.
      </a>
      ) from the University of Chile. Their model included endorphins, neurotransmitters of the
      <a href="/wiki/Limbic_system" title="Limbic system">
       limbic system
      </a>
      , the temporal lobe and other parts of the brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Extensions and variations of their model came from other scientists such as Louis Appleby (1989) and Karl Jansen (1990).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Morse
      <i>
       et al
      </i>
      . 1989 proposed a neurophysiological model in which
      <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">
       serotonin
      </a>
      has an important role to play in generating NDEs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Home_Anesthetic.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1869" data-file-width="1974" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Home_Anesthetic.jpg/220px-Home_Anesthetic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Home_Anesthetic.jpg/330px-Home_Anesthetic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Home_Anesthetic.jpg/440px-Home_Anesthetic.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Home_Anesthetic.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">
         Ketamine
        </a>
        by intravenous injection can reproduce all the features of the NDE.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The research of Karl Jansen has revealed how the effects of an NDE can be induced by
      <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">
       ketamine
      </a>
      . In 1996 he published a paper on the subject which concluded "mounting evidence suggests that the reproduction/induction of NDE's by ketamine is not simply an interesting coincidence... ketamine administered by intravenous injection, in appropriate dosage, is capable of reproducing all of the features of the NDE which have been commonly described in the most cited works in this field."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Whinnery (1997) revealed the similarities between NDEs and
      <a href="/wiki/G-LOC" title="G-LOC">
       G-LOC
      </a>
      (G-force induced Loss Of Consciousness) episodes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whinnery_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Whinnery-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Based on the observations of G-LOC, Whinnery noted how the experiences often involved "tunnel vision and bright lights, floating sensations, automatic movement, autoscopy, OBEs, not wanting to be disturbed, paralysis, vivid dreamlets of beautiful places, pleasurable sensations, psychological alterations of euphoria and dissociation, inclusion of friends and family, inclusion of prior memories and thoughts, the experience being very memorable (when it can be remembered), confabulation, and a strong urge to understand the experience."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whinnery_78-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Whinnery-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1990s,
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Strassman" title="Rick Strassman">
       Rick Strassman
      </a>
      conducted research on the
      <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_drug" title="Psychedelic drug">
       psychedelic drug
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dimethyltryptamine" title="Dimethyltryptamine">
       dimethyltryptamine
      </a>
      (DMT) at the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Mexico" title="University of New Mexico">
       University of New Mexico
      </a>
      . Strassman advanced the hypothesis that a massive release of DMT from the
      <a href="/wiki/Pineal_gland" title="Pineal gland">
       pineal gland
      </a>
      prior to death or near-death was the cause of the near-death experience phenomenon. Only two of his test subjects reported NDE-like aural or visual hallucinations, although many reported feeling as though they had entered a state similar to the classical NDE. His explanation for this was the possible lack of panic involved in the clinical setting and possible dosage differences between those administered and those encountered in actual NDE cases. All subjects in the study were also very experienced users of DMT or other psychedelic/
      <a href="/wiki/Entheogen" title="Entheogen">
       entheogenic
      </a>
      agents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
       Chris French
      </a>
      (2001) stated that at least some reports of NDEs might be based upon
      <a href="/wiki/False_memory_syndrome" title="False memory syndrome">
       false memories
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to Engmann (2008) near-death experiences of people who are clinically dead are psychopathological symptoms caused by a severe malfunction of the brain resulting from the cessation of cerebral blood circulation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An important question is whether it is possible to "translate" the bloomy experiences of the reanimated survivors into psychopathologically basic phenomena, e.g. acoasms (nonverbal auditory hallucinations), central narrowing of the visual field,
      <a href="/wiki/Autoscopy" title="Autoscopy">
       autoscopia
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_hallucinations" title="Visual hallucinations">
       visual hallucinations
      </a>
      , activation of limbic and memory structures according to Moody's stages. The symptoms suppose a primary affliction of the
      <a href="/wiki/Occipital_lobe" title="Occipital lobe">
       occipital
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Temporal_lobe" title="Temporal lobe">
       temporal
      </a>
      cortices under clinical death. This basis could be congruent with the thesis of
      <a href="/wiki/Pathoclisis" title="Pathoclisis">
       pathoclisis
      </a>
      the inclination of special parts of the brain to be the first to be damaged in case of disease, lack of oxygen, or malnutritionestablished eighty years ago by
      <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9cile_Vogt-Mugnier" title="Ccile Vogt-Mugnier">
       Ccile
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Vogt" title="Oskar Vogt">
       Oskar Vogt
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Research has shown that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypercarbia" title="Hypercarbia">
       hypercarbia
      </a>
      can induce NDE symptoms such as lights, visions and mystical experiences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Professor of neurology
      <a href="/wiki/Terence_Hines" title="Terence Hines">
       Terence Hines
      </a>
      (2003) claimed that near-death experiences are hallucinations caused by
      <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hypoxia" title="Cerebral hypoxia">
       cerebral anoxia
      </a>
      , drugs, or brain damage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 2006 study by Lempert
      <i>
       et al
      </i>
      . induced
      <a href="/wiki/Syncope_(medicine)" title="Syncope (medicine)">
       syncopes
      </a>
      in 42 healthy subjects using cardiovascular manipulations. They found that the subjects reported NDE experiences such as seeing lights, tunnels, meeting deceased family members and visiting other worlds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Neuroscientists Olaf Blanke and Sebastian Dieguez (2009) have written that NDE experiences can best be explained by different brain functions and mechanisms without recourse to the paranormal. They suggest that damage to the bilateral
      <a href="/wiki/Occipital_lobe" title="Occipital lobe">
       occipital cortex
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Optic_radiation" title="Optic radiation">
       optic radiation
      </a>
      may lead to visual features of NDEs such as seeing a tunnel or lights, and interference with the
      <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">
       hippocampus
      </a>
      may lead to emotional experiences, memory flashbacks or a life review. They concluded that future neuroscientific studies are likely to reveal the neuroanatomical basis of the NDE which will lead to the demystification of the subject.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Vanhaudenhuyse
      <i>
       et al
      </i>
      . 2009 reported that recent studies employing
      <a href="/wiki/Deep_brain_stimulation" title="Deep brain stimulation">
       deep brain stimulation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Neuroimaging" title="Neuroimaging">
       neuroimaging
      </a>
      have demonstrated that out-of-body experiences result from a deficient
      <a href="/wiki/Multisensory_integration" title="Multisensory integration">
       multisensory integration
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Temporoparietal_junction" title="Temporoparietal junction">
       temporoparietal junction
      </a>
      and that ongoing studies aim to further identify the functional neuroanatomy of near-death experiences by means of standardized EEG recordings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Lakhmir Chawla, an Associate Professor of Anesthesiology and Critical Care Medicine and Medicine at
      <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University" title="George Washington University">
       George Washington University
      </a>
      medical centre argued that near-death experiences are caused by a surge of electrical activity as the brain runs out of oxygen before death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chawla_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chawla-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Levels of brain activity were similar to those seen in fully conscious people, even though blood pressure was so low as to be undetectable. The gradual loss of brain activity had occurred in the approximate hour before death, and was interrupted by a brief spurt of action, lasting from 30 seconds to three minutes. Chawla and colleagues from a case series of seven patients wrote "increase in electrical activity occurred when there was no discernable blood pressure, patients who suffer "near death" experiences may be recalling the aggregate memory of the synaptic activity associated with this terminal but potentially reversible hypoxemia."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chawla_90-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chawla-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Research released in 2010 by University of Maribor, Slovenia had put near-death experiences down to high levels of carbon dioxide in the blood altering the chemical balance of the brain and tricking it into 'seeing' things.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of the 52 patients, 11 reported NDEs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.nationalgeographic.com_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-news.nationalgeographic.com-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temporal_lobe_animation.gif">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Temporal_lobe_animation.gif/160px-Temporal_lobe_animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Temporal_lobe_animation.gif/240px-Temporal_lobe_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Temporal_lobe_animation.gif 2x" width="160"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Temporal_lobe_animation.gif" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Animation of the human left temporal lobe
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      NDE subjects have increased activity in the left
      <a href="/wiki/Temporal_lobe" title="Temporal lobe">
       temporal lobe
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britton.26Bootzin_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Britton.26Bootzin-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stimulation of the temporal lobe is known to induce hallucinations, out-of-body experiences and memory flashbacks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In an experiment with one patient, electrical stimulation at the left temporoparietal junction lead to an illusion of another person being close to her.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hopkin_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hopkin-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
       Chris French
      </a>
      has written that the "temporal lobe is almost certain to be involved in NDEs, given that both damage to and direct cortical stimulation of this area are known to produce a number of experiences corresponding to those of the NDE, including OBEs, hallucinations, and memory flashbacks."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2011, Alexander Wutzler and his colleagues at the
      <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charit">
       Charit University of Medicine
      </a>
      in Berlin, Germany suggested that near-death experiences may be triggered by an increase of
      <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">
       serotonin
      </a>
      in the brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Charles Q. Choi in an article for the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">
        Scientific American
       </a>
      </i>
      concluded "scientific evidence suggests that all features of the near-death experience have some basis in normal brain function gone awry."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A 2012 study led by neuroradiologist Renemane reached the conclusion that the NDE is a state of unconsciousness resembling
      <a href="/wiki/Oneiroid_syndrome" title="Oneiroid syndrome">
       oneiroid syndrome
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a 2013 study, Marie Thonnard and colleagues suggested that the memories of NDEs are
      <a href="/wiki/Flashbulb_memory" title="Flashbulb memory">
       flashbulb memories
      </a>
      of hallucinations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The findings were in accordance with a 2014 study published in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontiers_(publisher)" title="Frontiers (publisher)">
       Frontiers
      </a>
      in Human Neuroscience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="REM_state">
       REM state
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: REM state">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      It is suggested that the extreme stress caused by a life-threatening situation triggers brain states similar to
      <a href="/wiki/Rapid_eye_movement_sleep" title="Rapid eye movement sleep">
       REM sleep
      </a>
      and that a part of the near death experience is a state similar to dreaming while awake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      People who have experienced times when their brains behaved as if they were dreaming while awake are more likely to develop the near death experience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Lucid_dreaming">
       Lucid dreaming
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Lucid dreaming">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Some sleep researchers, such as Timothy J. Green, Lynne Levitan and
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_LaBerge" title="Stephen LaBerge">
       Stephen LaBerge
      </a>
      , have noted that NDEs are similar to many reports of
      <a href="/wiki/Lucid_dream" title="Lucid dream">
       lucid dreaming
      </a>
      , in which the individual realizes he is in a dream. Often these states are so realistic as to be barely distinguishable from reality.
     </p>
     <p>
      In a study of fourteen lucid dreamers performed in 1991, people who perform wake-initiated lucid dreams (WILD) reported experiences consistent with aspects of out-of-body experiences such as floating above their beds and the feeling of leaving their bodies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ldobe_105-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ldobe-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to the
      <a href="/wiki/Phenomenology_(psychology)" title="Phenomenology (psychology)">
       phenomenological
      </a>
      overlap between lucid dreams, near-death experiences, and
      <a href="/wiki/Out-of-body_experience" title="Out-of-body experience">
       out-of-body experiences
      </a>
      , researchers say they believe a protocol could be developed to induce a lucid dream similar to a near-death experience in the laboratory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Computational_psychology">
       Computational psychology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Computational psychology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Modeling of NDEs by S. L. Thaler in 1993
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      using
      <a href="/wiki/Artificial_neural_network" title="Artificial neural network">
       artificial neural networks
      </a>
      has shown that many aspects of the core near-death experience can be achieved through simulated neuron death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
