      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the course of such simulations, the essential features of the NDElife review, novel scenarios (i.e.,
      <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">
       heaven
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Hell" title="Hell">
       hell
      </a>
      ), and OBEare observed through the generation of confabulations or false memories, as discussed in
      <a href="/wiki/Confabulation_(neural_networks)" title="Confabulation (neural networks)">
       Confabulation (neural networks)
      </a>
      . The key feature contributing to the generation of such confabulatory states are a neural network's inability to differentiate dead from silent neurons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Memories, whether related to direct experience, or not, can be seeded upon arrays of such inactive brain cells.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">
       Effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      NDEs are also associated with changes in personality and outlook on life.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenneth Ring (professor of psychology) has identified a consistent set of value and belief changes associated with people who have had a near-death experience. Among these changes one finds a greater appreciation for life, higher self-esteem, greater compassion for others, a heightened sense of purpose and self-understanding, desire to learn, elevated spirituality, greater ecological sensitivity and planetary concern, and a feeling of being more intuitive. Changes may also include increased physical sensitivity; diminished tolerance of light, alcohol, and drugs; a feeling that the brain has been "altered" to encompass more; and a feeling that one is now using the "whole brain" rather than a small part.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mauro.2C_James_1992_15-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mauro.2C_James_1992-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, not all after-effects are beneficial
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Greyson
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      describes circumstances where changes in attitudes and behavior can lead to psychosocial and psychospiritual problems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Often the problems are those of the adjustment to ordinary life in the wake of the NDE.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-cultural_research">
       Cross-cultural research
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cross-cultural research">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Recent research into afterlife conceptions across cultures by religious studies scholar Gregory Shushan
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      analyzes the afterlife beliefs of five ancient civilizations (Old and Middle Kingdom Egypt, Sumerian and Old Babylonian Mesopotamia, Vedic India, pre-Buddhist China, and pre-Columbian Mesoamerica) in light of historical and contemporary reports of near-death experiences, and
      <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">
       shamanic
      </a>
      afterlife "journeys". It was found that despite numerous culture-specific differences, the nine most frequently recurring NDE elements also recur on a general structural level cross-culturally, which tends to suggest that the authors of these ancient religious texts were familiar with NDEs or similar experiences. Cross-cultural similarity, however, can be used to support both religious and physiological theories, for both rely on demonstrating that the phenomenon is universal.
     </p>
     <p>
      Studies that have investigated cultural differences in NDEs summarized by (Augustine, 2003) have argued that the content of the experiences do not vary by culture, except for the identity of the figures seen during the experiences. For example, a
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christian
      </a>
      may see
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">
       Jesus
      </a>
      , while a
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hindu
      </a>
      may see
      <a href="/wiki/Yama_(Hinduism)" title="Yama (Hinduism)">
       Yamaraja
      </a>
      , the Hindu king of death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infidels.org_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-infidels.org-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Van_Lommel_studies">
       Van Lommel studies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Van Lommel studies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:173px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1125" data-file-width="768" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg/171px-Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg/256px-Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg/341px-Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg 2x" width="171"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pim_van_Lommel-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Pim_van_Lommel" title="Pim van Lommel">
         Pim van Lommel
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2001,
      <a href="/wiki/Pim_van_Lommel" title="Pim van Lommel">
       Pim van Lommel
      </a>
      , a cardiologist from the Netherlands, and his team conducted a study of near-death experiences (NDEs) in
      <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrest" title="Cardiac arrest">
       cardiac arrest
      </a>
      patients.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lommel_P_2001_63-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lommel_P_2001-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of 344 patients who were successfully resuscitated after suffering cardiac arrest, 62 (18%) expressed an intraoperative memory and among these, 41 (12%) experienced core NDEs, which included
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out-of-body_experiences" title="Out-of-body experiences">
       out-of-body experiences
      </a>
      . According to van Lommel, the patients remembered details of their conditions during their cardiac arrest despite being clinically dead with flatlined brain stem activity. Van Lommel concluded that his findings supported the theory that
      <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">
       consciousness
      </a>
      continued despite lack of neuronal activity in the brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lommel_P_2001_63-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lommel_P_2001-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Van Lommel's conclusions have been criticized by various authors, one of them being Jason Braithwaite, a Senior Lecturer in Cognitive Neuroscience in the Behavioral Brain Sciences Centre,
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">
       University of Birmingham
      </a>
      . He issued an in-depth analysis and critique of van Lommel's prospective study published in the medical journal
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">
        The Lancet
       </a>
      </i>
      , concluding that while van Lommel's et al. study makes a useful contribution, it contains several factual and logical errors. Among these errors are van Lommel's misunderstandings and misinterpretations of the dying-brain hypothesis, misunderstandings over the role of anoxia, misplaced confidence in EEG measurements (a flat electroencephalogram (EEG) reading is not evidence of total brain inactivity), etc. Braithwaite concluded with, "it is difficult to see what one could learn from the paranormal survivalist position which sets out assuming the truth of that which it seeks to establish, makes additional and unnecessary assumptions, misrepresents the current state of knowledge from mainstream science, and appears less than comprehensive in its analysis of the available facts."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Braithwaite_2008_54-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Braithwaite_2008-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="AWARE_study">
       AWARE study
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: AWARE study">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 2001,
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Parnia" title="Sam Parnia">
       Sam Parnia
      </a>
      and colleagues investigated out-of-body claims by placing figures on suspended boards facing the ceiling, not visible from the floor. Parnia wrote "anybody who claimed to have left their body and be near the ceiling during resuscitation attempts would be expected to identify those targets. If, however, such perceptions are psychological, then one would obviously not expect the targets to be identified."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The philosopher Keith Augustine, who examined Parnia's study, has written that all target identification experiments have produced negative results.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infidels.org_117-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-infidels.org-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Psychologist
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
       Chris French
      </a>
      wrote regarding the study "unfortunately, and somewhat atypically, none of the survivors in this sample experienced an OBE."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the autumn of 2008, 25 UK and US hospitals began participation in a study, coordinated by Sam Parnia and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southampton_University" title="Southampton University">
       Southampton University
      </a>
      known as the AWARE study (AWAreness during REsuscitation). Following on from the work of
      <a href="/wiki/Pim_van_Lommel" title="Pim van Lommel">
       Pim van Lommel
      </a>
      in the Netherlands, the study aims to examine near-death experiences in 1,500
      <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrest" title="Cardiac arrest">
       cardiac arrest
      </a>
      survivors and so determine whether people without a heartbeat or brain activity can have documentable out-of-body experiences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dreaper2008_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dreaper2008-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As part of the study Parnia and colleagues have investigated out of body claims by using hidden targets placed on shelves that could only be seen from above.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dreaper2008_119-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dreaper2008-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Parnia has written "if no one sees the pictures, it shows these experiences are illusions or false memories".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dreaper2008_119-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dreaper2008-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2014 Parnia issued a statement indicating that the first phase of the project has been completed and the results are undergoing peer review for publication in a medical journal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      No subjects saw the images mounted out of sight according to Parnia's early report of the results of the study at an
      <a href="/wiki/American_Heart_Association" title="American Heart Association">
       American Heart Association
      </a>
      meeting in November 2013. Only two out of the 152 patients reported any visual experiences, and one of them described events that could be verified.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 6, 2014 the results of the study were published in the journal
      <i>
       Resuscitation
      </i>
      . Among those who reported a perception of awareness and completed further interviews, 46 per cent experienced a broad range of mental recollections in relation to death that were not compatible with the commonly used term of NDEs. These included fearful and persecutory experiences. Only 9 per cent had experiences compatible with NDEs and 2 per cent exhibited full awareness compatible with OBEs with explicit recall of 'seeing' and 'hearing' events. One case was validated and timed using auditory stimuli during cardiac arrest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Dr. Caroline Watt "The one verifiable period of conscious awareness that Parnia was able to report did not relate to this objective test. Rather, it was a patient giving a supposedly accurate report of events during his resuscitation. He didnt identify the pictures, he described the defibrillator machine noise. But thats not very impressive since many people know what goes on in an emergency room setting from seeing recreations on television."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      And according to
      <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">
       clinical neurologist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Steven_Novella" title="Steven Novella">
       Steven Novella
      </a>
      , Parnia is "desperately trying to rescue the study by falling back on simply reporting subjective accounts of what people remember long after the event. This type of information is nothing new, and cannot objectively resolve the debate. The results are also completely unimpressive, perfectly consistent with what we would expect given what is already well documented about human memory."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      AWARE II - a two-year multicenter observational study of 900-1500 patients experiencing cardiac arrests is currently being prepared, with the closure date set to May 31, 2016.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Afterlife_claims_and_skeptical_responses">
       Afterlife claims and skeptical responses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Afterlife claims and skeptical responses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Consciousness_after_death" title="Consciousness after death">
       Consciousness after death
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Many individuals who experience an NDE see it as a verification of the existence of an
      <a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">
       afterlife
      </a>
      , and some researchers in the field of
      <a href="/wiki/Near-death_studies" title="Near-death studies">
       near-death studies
      </a>
      see the NDE as evidence that human
      <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">
       consciousness
      </a>
      may continue to exist after death. The transcendental (or survivalist) interpretation of the NDE contends that the experience is exactly what it appears to be to the persons having the experience. According to this interpretation, consciousness can become separated from the
      <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">
       brain
      </a>
      under certain conditions and glimpse the spiritual realm to which
      <a href="/wiki/Soul" title="Soul">
       souls
      </a>
      travel after death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www-new1.heacademy.ac.uk_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-www-new1.heacademy.ac.uk-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The transcendental model is in some friction with the dominant view from mainstream
      <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">
       neuroscience
      </a>
      ; that consciousness is a product of, and dependent on, the brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the mainstream neuroscientific view, once the brain stops functioning at
      <a href="/wiki/Brain_death" title="Brain death">
       brain death
      </a>
      , consciousness fails to survive and ceases to exist.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Several NDE researchers have argued that the NDE poses a major challenge to current scientific thinking regarding the relationship between consciousness and the brain, as argued by
      <a href="/wiki/Pim_van_Lommel" title="Pim van Lommel">
       Van Lommel
      </a>
      :
     </p>
     <table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
      <tr>
       <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
        
       </td>
       <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
        How could a clear consciousness outside ones body be experienced at the moment that the brain no longer functions during a period of
        <a href="/wiki/Clinical_death" title="Clinical death">
         clinical death
        </a>
        with flat
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EEG" title="EEG">
         EEG
        </a>
        ?... (the) NDE pushes at the limits of medical ideas about the range of human consciousness and the mind-brain relation.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lommel_P_2001_63-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Lommel_P_2001-63">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          63
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
        
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Other NDE researchers such as
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Parnia" title="Sam Parnia">
       Parnia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Fenwick_(neuropsychologist)" title="Peter Fenwick (neuropsychologist)">
       Fenwick
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-horizonresearch.org_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-horizonresearch.org-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Greyson" title="Bruce Greyson">
       Greyson
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      have expressed similar questions and concerns.
     </p>
     <p>
      These arguments raised by several researchers have been criticized by some
      <a href="/wiki/Scientific_skepticism" title="Scientific skepticism">
       scientific skeptics
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Scientist" title="Scientist">
       scientists
      </a>
      on several grounds.
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
       Chris French
      </a>
      (2005, 2009) noted that, "it is clear that the argument that recent findings present a major challenge to modern neuroscience hinges upon the claim that the NDE is actually experienced "during a period of clinical death with flat EEG" as claimed". With respect to the former point he pointed out that it is not at all clear that NDEs actually do occur during a period of flat EEG. Assuming that the patients in question entered a period of flat EEG, French argued that the NDE may have occurred as they entered that state or as they slowly recovered from it. Parnia and Fenwick (2001) had rejected the idea that the NDE may have occurred as the patient is becoming unconscious because they argued that this happens too quickly. But French points out that it is unclear how much time would be required to experience an NDE and that a common feature of
      <a href="/wiki/Altered_state_of_consciousness" title="Altered state of consciousness">
       altered states of consciousness
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Time_perception" title="Time perception">
       time distortion
      </a>
      . He argued that this is well illustrated by the life review component of the NDE itself which, although involving a review of a persons entire life, only seems to last a very brief time. And that therefore, "who can say, therefore, that the few seconds of remaining consciousness as an individual enters the state of clinical death is insufficient for the experiences that form the basis of the NDE?".
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg">
        <img alt=" photo of Chris French presenting from podium at the World Skeptics Congress 2012 in Berlin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg/220px-Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg/330px-Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg/440px-Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chris_French_World_Skeptics_Congress_Berlin_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Chris_French" title="Chris French">
         Chris French
        </a>
        a notable skeptic of the afterlife claims of NDErs
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Parnia and Fenwick (2001) also claimed that the NDE could not occur as a person slowly regains consciousness as this period is characterized by
      <a href="/wiki/Delirium" title="Delirium">
       delirium
      </a>
      and not by the lucid consciousness reported by NDErs. French again argued that the attribution of confusion is typically made by an outside observer. The subjects themselves may not subjectively feel confused at all. He quoted from an article by Liere and Stickney where they noted that, Hypoxia quickly affects the higher centers, causing a blunting of the finer sensibilities and a loss of sense of judgment and of self-criticism. The subject feels, however, that his mind is not only quite clear, but unusually keen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and that the subjective claim of great clarity of thought may therefore well be an illusion. French (2005) also noted that "it should be borne in mind that we are always dealing with reports of experiences rather than with the experiences themselves. Memory is a reconstructive process. It is highly likely the final narrative will be much more coherent after the individual has reflected upon it before telling it to others, given the inherently ineffable nature of the experience itself".
     </p>
     <p>
      And with respect to the latter point, the survivalists have also been criticized by scientists like French and Braithwaite of placing undue confidence in EEG measures. French (2005, 2009) and Braithwaite (2008) claimed that survivalists generally appear to assume that a flat EEG is indicative of total brain inactivity and that therefore the experience of an NDE during such a flatline period would completely undermine the core assumption of modern neuroscience that any complex experience must be based upon a functioning neural substrate.
     </p>
     <p>
      Even assuming that NDEs actually occur during such periods, the assumption that isoelectric surface EEG recordings are always indicative of total brain inactivity is according to Braithwaite and French wrong. Braithwaite noted that "unless surgically implanted into the brain directly, the EEG principally measures surface cortical activity. The waveforms seen in cortical EEG are largely regarded to come from the synchronistic firing of cortical pyramidal neurons. As such, it is entirely conceivable that deep sub-cortical brain structures could be firing, and even in seizure, in the absence of any cortical signs of this activity."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Braithwaite_2008_54-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Braithwaite_2008-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Braithwaite also noted that Gloor (1986) reviewed evidence indicating that inter-ictal discharges in the
      <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">
       hippocampus
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Amygdala" title="Amygdala">
       amygdala
      </a>
      can produce complex meaningful hallucinations without the involvement of the
      <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_cortex" title="Cerebral cortex">
       cerebral cortex
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Another argument which, according to Braithwaite (2008), relies upon misplaced confidence in surface EEG measurement was put forward by Fenwick P. and Fenwick E. (1995).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They argued that, in cases where the surface EEG recording was not flat, if the NDE was a hallucinatory experience based upon disinhibition, evidence of this disinhibition should be visible in the surface EEG recorded at the time. However, Braithwaite argued that data from a recent study comparing EEG recorded at the scalp with EEG recorded from electrodes surgically implanted in deep sub-cortical regions show conclusively that high-amplitude seizure activity can be occurring in deep brain regions and yet be completely undetectable in the surface EEG.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Even more so, a study comparing surface EEG recordings with the fMRI blood-oxygen-level dependent (BOLD) response showed that the surface EEG could fail to detect
      <a href="/wiki/Epileptic_seizure" title="Epileptic seizure">
       seizure activity
      </a>
      at the level of the cortex that was detected by the BOLD response.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Another argument made by several NDE researchers such as Parnia and Fenwick (2001) for the transcendental model is that the occurrence of
      <a href="/wiki/Anecdotal_evidence" title="Anecdotal evidence">
       anecdotal reports
      </a>
      of patients being able to see and recall detailed events occurring during the cardiac arrest that are afterwards verified by hospital staff supports the argument that such perception sometimes do occur during periods of clinical death. NDE researcher Janice Miner Holden found 107 such anecdotal reports in the NDE literature as of 2009, out of which approximately 91% were accurate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to French (2005) and
      <a href="/wiki/Susan_Blackmore" title="Susan Blackmore">
       Blackmore
      </a>
      (1993), when serious attempts at corroboration are attempted, the evidence often turns out to be nowhere near as impressive as it initially appeared.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      And such cases can possibly (since they had not been ruled out) be accounted for in terms of non-paranormal factors including, "information available at the time, prior knowledge, fantasy or dreams, lucky guesses, and information from the remaining senses. Then there is selective memory for correct details, incorporation of details learned between the end of the NDE and giving an account of it, and the tendency to tell a good story.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to French (2005) a similar claim to the argument from veridical perceptions are the cases of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blindness" title="Blindness">
       blind
      </a>
      people that during NDEs are able to see even though, in some cases, they may have been blind from birth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to French (2005), "initial readings of such accounts often give the impression that the experience involves seeing events and surroundings in the same way that sighted people do, but closer reflection upon these cases suggests otherwise." French quoted from an article by NDE researcher
      <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Ring" title="Kenneth Ring">
       Ring
      </a>
      where he noted that, "as this kind of testimony builds, it seems more and more difficult to claim that the blind simply see what they report. Rather, it is beginning to appear it is more a matter of their knowing, through a still poorly understood mode of generalized awareness, based on a variety of sensory impressions, especially tactile ones, what is happening around them."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      French (2005) concluded that, "NDEs in the blind are certainly worthy of study but do not merit any special status in terms of evidential support for spiritual explanations of the phenomenon."
     </p>
     <p>
      Nevertheless, according to French (2005) future research in the near-death experience should focus on devising ways to distinguish between the two main hypotheses relating to when the NDE is occurring.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      If it really is occurring when some NDE researchers claim that it is, during a period of flat EEG with no cortical activity, then modern neuroscience would require serious revision.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This would also be the case if the OBE, either within the NDE or not, could be shown to be veridical. Attempts to test the veridicality of OBEs using hidden targets (e.g., Parnia and Fenwick (2001) should be welcomed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French2005_65-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-French2005-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_experiences">
       Personal experiences
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personal experiences">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Return_from_Tomorrow" title="Return from Tomorrow">
         Return from Tomorrow
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/George_G._Ritchie" title="George G. Ritchie">
        George G. Ritchie
       </a>
       with Elizabeth Sherrill (1978). At the age of 20, George Ritchie died in an army hospital. Nine minutes later he returned to life. Ritchie's story was the first contact
       <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Moody" title="Raymond Moody">
        Raymond Moody
       </a>
       (who was studying at the University of Virginia, as an undergraduate in Philosophy, at the time) had with NDEs. It inspired Moody to investigate over 150 cases of near-death experiences, in his book
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Life_After_Life_(book)" title="Life After Life (book)">
         Life After Life
        </a>
       </i>
       , and two other books that followed.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embraced_by_the_Light" title="Embraced by the Light">
         Embraced by the Light
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Betty_Eadie" title="Betty Eadie">
        Betty Eadie
       </a>
       (1992). One of the most detailed near-death experiences on record.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Saved_by_the_Light" title="Saved by the Light">
         Saved by the Light
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Dannion_Brinkley" title="Dannion Brinkley">
        Dannion Brinkley
       </a>
       . Brinkley's experience documents one of the most complete near death experiences, in terms of core experience and additional phenomena from the NDE scale. Brinkley claims to have been clinically dead for 28 minutes and taken to a hospital morgue, but some of his claims are disputed.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Placebo_(at_funeral)" title="Placebo (at funeral)">
         Placebo
        </a>
       </i>
       by Howard Pittman (1980). A detailed record of Pittman's near-death experience.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Darkness of God
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Wren-Lewis" title="John Wren-Lewis">
        John Wren-Lewis
       </a>
       (1985). Bulletin of the Australian Institute for Psychical Research No 5. An account of the effects of his NDE after going through the death process several times in one night.
      </li>
      <li>
       Three have associated their experiences with their decision to join the
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah' Faith">
        Bah' Faith
       </a>
       : Reinee Pasarow, Ricky Bradshaw, and Marie Watson. Pasarow's published her story as early as 1981.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         144
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       At least one extended talk was video taped and is available online in a couple places.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         145
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also extended partial transcripts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         146
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bradshaw's experience has been reviewed in several books.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         147
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         148
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         149
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Watson, author of
       <i>
        Two Paths
       </i>
       in 1897,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         150
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       says she suffered a car accident in 1890 in Washington DC and reported having a vision and met a guide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         151
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       She converted to the religion in 1901 and identified the guide as `Abdu'l-Bah.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dying_to_be_Me_(book)" title="Dying to be Me (book)">
        Dying To Be Me
       </a>
       : My Journey from Cancer, to Near Death, to True Healing by
       <a href="/wiki/Anita_Moorjani" title="Anita Moorjani">
        Anita Moorjani
       </a>
       , an ethnic Indian woman from Hong Kong, experienced a NDE which has been documented on the Near Death Experience Research Foundation (NDERF) website as one of the most exceptional accounts on their archives. She had end-stage cancer and on February 2, 2006, doctors told her family that she only had a few hours to live. Following her NDE, Anita experienced a remarkable recovery of her health.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         152
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kiki_Carter" title="Kiki Carter">
        Kiki Carter
       </a>
       , a.k.a.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kimberli_Wilson" title="Kimberli Wilson">
        Kimberli Wilson
       </a>
       , an environmental activist and singer/songwriter, reported a near-death experience in 1983. The day after the experience, her mother, Priscilla Greenwood, encouraged her to write it down. Priscilla Greenwood published the story in September 1983 in a local metaphysical journal. For 24 hours after the experience, Kimberli had an aftervision which was a catalyst for her interest in quantum physics and holograms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         153
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/90_Minutes_in_Heaven" title="90 Minutes in Heaven">
         90 Minutes in Heaven
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_Piper" title="Don Piper">
        Don Piper
       </a>
       , is Piper's account of his own near-death experience. EMTs on the scene determined Piper had been killed instantly after a tractor-trailer had swerved into his lane, crushing his car. Piper survived, however. In the book, he wrote about seeing deceased loved ones and friends as well as magnificent light; he felt a sense of pure peace. Piper had a very difficult and painful recovery, undergoing 34 surgeries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         154
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Heaven_Is_for_Real" title="Heaven Is for Real">
         Heaven Is for Real
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Todd_Burpo" title="Todd Burpo">
        Todd Burpo
       </a>
       , is a father's account of his son, Colton, and Colton's trip to heaven and back. After discovering that then-four-year-old Colton's appendix has ruptured, he was rushed to the hospital. While unconscious, Colton describes having met Jesus, God, his great-grandfather whom he had never met, and his older sister lost in a miscarriage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         155
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parallel_Universes,_a_Memoir_from_the_Edges_of_Space_and_Time" title="Parallel Universes, a Memoir from the Edges of Space and Time">
         Parallel Universes, a Memoir from the Edges of Space and Time
        </a>
       </i>
       by Linda Morabito Meyer is a NASA scientist's account of several near death experiences at the hands of her parents and William Franklin Mosley of the Temple of the More Abundant Life in Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada. She explained that during these experiences, she visited Heaven, saw Jesus, and was in the presence of God.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         156
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Eben_Alexander_(author)" title="Eben Alexander (author)">
        Eben Alexander, M.D.
       </a>
       , born December, 1953, author of
       <i>
        Proof of Heaven: A Neurosurgeon's Journey into the Afterlife
       </i>
       , which made
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_list" title="The New York Times Best Seller list">
        <i>
         The New York Times
        </i>
        Best Seller list
       </a>
       for nonfiction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         157
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the book, Alexander describes how he had an intense NDE while in a seven-day coma brought on by an attack of
       <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">
        meningitis
       </a>
       . Inconsistencies and other issues in his story have led to questions about its veracity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         158
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Howard_Storm_(author)" title="Howard Storm (author)">
        Howard Storm
       </a>
       . In 1985, Storm travelled to Europe with his wife and university students. After suffering from severe stomach pain, he ended up in a hospital in
       <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
        Paris
       </a>
       , where he had a near-death experience.
      </li>
      <li>
       Curtis "Earthquake" Kelley experienced a near death experience after a drug overdose.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         159
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Josh_Homme" title="Josh Homme">
        Josh Homme
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Queens_of_the_Stone_Age" title="Queens of the Stone Age">
        Queens of the Stone Age
       </a>
       elaborated on his near-death experience in an interview with Marc Maron in October 2013. He told Maron that he contracted a
       <a href="/wiki/Methicillin-resistant_Staphylococcus_aureus" title="Methicillin-resistant Staphylococcus aureus">
        methicillin-resistant
        <i>
         Staphylococcus aureus
        </i>
       </a>
       (MRSA) infection in 2010, which his immune system could not fight due to stress. Due to unexpected complications during knee surgery, the doctors could not oxygenate his blood, and Josh suffered a near-death experience due to asphyxiation. Doctors eventually had to use a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defibrillator" title="Defibrillator">
        defibrillator
       </a>
       to revive him. Following this, he was confined to bed rest for three months. The experience left him weakened and unable to produce music for almost two years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         160
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">
       In popular culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In popular culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Near-death experiences have been a theme in several films, like
      <a href="/wiki/Hereafter_(film)" title="Hereafter (film)">
       <i>
        Hereafter
       </i>
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Clint_Eastwood" title="Clint Eastwood">
       Clint Eastwood
      </a>
      (2010) and
      <i>
       Stay
      </i>
      by Marc Forster (2008). It has also been a subject in fantastic literature, for example in the novella
      <i>
       The Baron Bagge
      </i>
      by Alexander Lernet-Holenia (1936).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also part of books written by
      <a href="/wiki/Karl_May" title="Karl May">
       Karl May
      </a>
      in his novels with the names 'the Hereafter' ('Am Jenseits',1899) and in 'In the Realm of the Silver lion III'('Im Reiche des silbernen Lwen II', 1902).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Films">
       Films
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Films">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ghost_(1990_film)" title="Ghost (1990 film)">
        Ghost
       </a>
       - starring
       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Swayze" title="Patrick Swayze">
        Patrick Swayze
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Demi_Moore" title="Demi Moore">
        Demi Moore
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Whoopi_Goldberg" title="Whoopi Goldberg">
        Whoopi Goldberg
       </a>
       . The film received several Academy Awards and Oscar nominations.
      </li>
      <li>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Known_NDE_researchers">
       Known NDE researchers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Known NDE researchers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Maurice_S._Rawlings">
       Maurice S. Rawlings
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Maurice S. Rawlings">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Maurice_S._Rawlings" title="Maurice S. Rawlings">
       Maurice S. Rawlings
      </a>
      was an American cardiologist and focused on professional and Christian point of view with near-death experiences. Rawlings was a doctor of President Eisenhower and the Joint Chiefs of Staff. He criticized other death investigators as Moody and Kbler-Ross, that the interviews with stakeholders never took place immediately after the revival, but usually several weeks after that. With timely interviews there were not only positive, but also negative (descent into hell) reports from the beyond what Moody and Kbler-Ross on sow. Rawlings was the author of several books, including: "Beyond the line of death - New clear evidence for the existence of Heaven and Hell" (1987), "To Hell and Back - Afterlife" (1996), which were translated into several languages.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Raymond_A._Moody">
       Raymond A. Moody
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Raymond A. Moody">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raymond_A._Moody" title="Raymond A. Moody">
       Raymond A. Moody
      </a>
      was one of the first to systematically examined the experiences of patients who were clinically dead and revived. He found a high correlation of plays.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Elisabeth_K.C3.BCbler-Ross">
       Elisabeth Kbler-Ross
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Elisabeth Kbler-Ross">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_K%C3%BCbler-Ross" title="Elisabeth Kbler-Ross">
       Elisabeth Kbler-Ross
      </a>
      interviewed numerous people who were dying and described in her work the "five stages of dying". This refers to how patients deal with the realization that they have to die soon. She also focused on near-death experiences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Medical Examiner Elisabeth Kbler-Ross was the first to publish interviews with dying in 1969 reports of near-death experiences in her book.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bernard_Jakoby">
       Bernard Jakoby
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bernard Jakoby">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Jakoby&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bernard Jakoby (page does not exist)">
       Bernard Jakoby
      </a>
      is a German death researcher who comes to similar conclusions as Moody.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pim_van_Lommel">
       Pim van Lommel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Pim van Lommel">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Pim_van_Lommel" title="Pim van Lommel">
       Pim van Lommel
      </a>
      is a cardiologist and lead prospective studies about NDE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sam_Parnia">
       Sam Parnia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sam Parnia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Parnia" title="Sam Parnia">
       Sam Parnia
      </a>
      is a British cardiologist who does research experiences at Weill Cornell Medical College in New York on near-death experiences and out of body. 2014 he published a study had been interviewed at the reanimated heart patients. 9 of 140 interviewed patients reported a near-death experience, according to the Greyson NDE Scale,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one of the two audio-visual perceptions immediately after the official cardiac arrest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bruce_Greyson">
       Bruce Greyson
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Near-death_experience&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Bruce Greyson">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Greyson" title="Bruce Greyson">
       Bruce Greyson
      </a>
      is an American psychiatrist and neuroscientist. He is Professor of Psychiatry and Director Division of Perceptual Studies at the University of Virginia and therefore the direct successor to Ian Stevenson. He is a founding member of the International Association for Near-Death Studies (IANDS) and is known for his work in the field of near-death experience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He developed 1983 Greyson questionnaire for the qualification of a near-death experience ("Greyson's NDE scale").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

       <li id="cite_note-ldobe-105">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-ldobe_105-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Lynne Levitan; Stephen LaBerge (1991).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lucidity.com/NL32.OBEandLD.html" rel="nofollow">
           "Other Worlds: Out-of-Body Experiences and Lucid Dreams"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Nightlight
          </i>
          (The Lucidity Institute)
          <b>
           3
          </b>
          (2-3).
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANear-death+experience&amp;rft.atitle=Other+Worlds%3A+Out-of-Body+Experiences+and+Lucid+Dreams&amp;rft.aulast=Lynne+Levitan&amp;rft.au=Lynne+Levitan&amp;rft.au=Stephen+LaBerge&amp;rft.date=1991&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lucidity.com%2FNL32.OBEandLD.html&amp;rft.issue=2-3&amp;rft.jtitle=Nightlight&amp;rft.pub=The+Lucidity+Institute&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=3">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-106">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-106">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Green, J. Timothy (1995). "Lucid dreams as one method of replicating components of the near-death experience in a laboratory setting".
          <i>
           Journal-of-Near-Death-Studies
          </i>
          <b>
           14
          </b>
          : 49.
          <q>
           A large phenomenological overlap among lucid dreams, out-of-body experiences, and near-death experiences suggests the possibility of developing a methodology of replicating components of the near-death experience using newly developed methods of inducing lucid dreams. Reports on the literature of both spontaneous and induced near-death-experience-like episodes during lucid dreams suggest a possible protocol.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANear-death+experience&amp;rft.atitle=Lucid+dreams+as+one+method+of+replicating+components+of+the+near-death+experience+in+a+laboratory+setting&amp;rft.au=Green%2C+J.+Timothy&amp;rft.aulast=Green%2C+J.+Timothy&amp;rft.date=1995&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal-of-Near-Death-Studies&amp;rft.pages=49&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=14">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANear-death+experience&amp;rft.atitle=Chronic+disorders+of+consciousness&amp;rft.au=Bernat+JL&amp;rft.aulast=Bernat+JL&amp;rft.date=8+Apr+2006&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2FS0140-6736%2806%2968508-5&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F16616561&amp;rft.issue=9517&amp;rft.jtitle=Lancet&amp;rft.pages=1181-1192&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=367">

       <li id="cite_note-130">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-130">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Laureys, Steven; Tononi, Giulio (2009).
          <i>
           The Neurology of Consciousness: Cognitive Neuroscience and Neuropathology
          </i>
          (1st ed. ed.). Amsterdam: Elsevier Academic Press. p.20.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-12-374168-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-12-374168-4">
           978-0-12-374168-4
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           In brain death there is irreversible cessation of all functions of the brain including the brainstem. Consciousness is, therefore, permanently lost in brain death.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANear-death+experience&amp;rft.aufirst=Steven&amp;rft.aulast=Laureys&amp;rft.au=Laureys%2C+Steven&amp;rft.au=Tononi%2C+Giulio&amp;rft.btitle=The+Neurology+of+Consciousness%3A+Cognitive+Neuroscience+and+Neuropathology&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.edition=1st+ed.&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-12-374168-4&amp;rft.pages=20&amp;rft.place=Amsterdam&amp;rft.pub=Elsevier+Academic+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANear-death+experience&amp;rft.btitle=WTF+with+Marc+Maron+Podcast+-+Episode+431+-+Josh+Homme&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wtfpod.com%2Fpodcast%2Fepisodes%2Fepisode_431_-_josh_homme&amp;rft.pub=Wtfpod.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-161">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-161">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         compare Dietmar Czycholl (Hg.):
         <i>
          Als ich am gestrigen Tag entschlief. Erfahrungen Wiederbelebter in der Weltliteratur. Eine Anthologie aus drei Jahrtausenden
         </i>
         . Genius Verlag, Oberstaufen 2003
         <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3934719139">
          ISBN 3-934719-13-9
         </a>
        </span>

        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         <i>
          Am Jenseits
         </i>
         , Freiburg i.Br. 1912, S. 504 ff.
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.zeno.org/Literatur/M/May,+Karl/Reiseerz%C3%A4hlungen/Am+Jenseits/4.+Kapitel.+El+Aschdar" rel="nofollow">
          (online auf zeno.org)
         </a>
         ;
         <i>
          Im Reiche des silbernen Lwen
         </i>
         , Band 3, Freiburg i.Br. 1908, S. 270 ff.
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.zeno.org/Literatur/M/May,+Karl/Reiseerz%C3%A4hlungen/Im+Reiche+des+silbernen+L%C3%B6wen+III/3.+Kapitel.+Am+Tode" rel="nofollow">
          (online auf zeno.org)
         </a>
         .

          </i>
         </a>
         , abgerufen am 14. Mrz 2014

       <li id="cite_note-165">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-165">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.wissenschaft.de/home/-/journal_content/56/12054/62660/" rel="nofollow">
          <i>
           Bild der Wissenschaft: Sind Nahtod-Erfahrungen Bilder aus dem Jenseits?
          </i>
         </a>
         Ein helles Licht am Ende eines langen Tunnels, ein Gefhl von Freude und Hoffnung: Davon erzhlten Patienten, die einen Herzstillstand erlitten haben, britischen Forschern. Die Wissenschaftler der Universitt Southampton werten diese Berichte als die bislang schlssigsten Hinweise auf ein Leben nach dem Tod, schreibt die deutsche rzte-Zeitung.  abgerufen am 16. Mrz 2014.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-166">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-166">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         van Lommel P, van Wees R, Meyers V, Elfferich I. (2001) Near-Death Experience in Survivors of Cardiac Arrest: A prospective Study in the Netherlands,
         <i>
          The Lancet
         </i>
         , 358(9298):203945,
         <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
          doi
         </a>
         :
         <a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1016%2FS0140-6736%2801%2907100-8" rel="nofollow">
          10.1016/S0140-6736(01)07100-8
         </a>
         .
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-167">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

          <a href="#cite_ref-167">
           ^

        <span class="reference-text">

         <a class="external text" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15142300?dopt=Abstract" rel="nofollow">
          <i>
           A Rasch scaling validation of a 'core' near-death experience.
          </i>
         </a>
         NDE-Definition: "NDEs reflect peace, joy and harmony, followed by insight and mystical or religious experiences, while the most intense NDEs involve an awareness of things occurring in a different place or time.", published May 2004
        </span>

          <i>
           Bild der Wissenschaft: Sind Nahtod-Erfahrungen Bilder aus dem Jenseits?
          </i>
         </a>
         Ein helles Licht am Ende eines langen Tunnels, ein Gefhl von Freude und Hoffnung: Davon erzhlten Patienten, die einen Herzstillstand erlitten haben, britischen Forschern. Die Wissenschaftler der Universitt Southampton werten diese Berichte als die bislang schlssigsten Hinweise auf ein Leben nach dem Tod, schreibt die deutsche rzte-Zeitung. und Eines macht der Forscher Bruce Greyson von der Universitt Virginia klar: Menschen mit Nahtod-Erlebnissen sind nicht psychisch krank. Die nderung des Bewusstseins fhrt nicht zu bleibenden Schden, berichtete er in der Fachzeitschrift Lancet (Bd. 355, S. 460). abgerufen am 16. Mrz 2014.
